  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2e9bf5f3-1187-4f5d-a281-0a7bec5fb143'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9341526509363836213">In this heartbreaking Turkish novel based on the real-life sinking of a refugee ship during World War II, an elderly professor leaves America to revisit the city where he last glimpsed his beloved wife. <br/><br/>Istanbul, 2001. Maya Duran is a single mother struggling to balance a demanding job at Istanbul University with the challenges of raising a teenage son. Her worries increas</span>
  <span id="freeText9341526509363836213" style="display:none">In this heartbreaking Turkish novel based on the real-life sinking of a refugee ship during World War II, an elderly professor leaves America to revisit the city where he last glimpsed his beloved wife. <br /><br />Istanbul, 2001. Maya Duran is a single mother struggling to balance a demanding job at Istanbul University with the challenges of raising a teenage son. Her worries increase when she is tasked with looking after the enigmatic Maximilian Wagner, an elderly German-born Harvard professor visiting the city at the university's invitation. Although he is distant at first, Maya gradually learns of the tragic circumstances that brought him to Istanbul sixty years before, and the dark realities that continue to haunt him. <br /><br />Inspired by the 1942 Struma disaster, in which nearly 800 Jewish refugees perished after the ship carrying them to Palestine was torpedoed off the coast of Turkey, Serenade for Nadia is both a poignant love story and a gripping testament to the power of human connection in crisis.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9341526509363836213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_52256788').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_52256788').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_52256788').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781635420166" href="/book/show/52256788-serenade-for-nadia">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7209729-lilisa?shelf=lin">lin</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3148291553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16699253787283365733">A lovely historical fiction based on the sinking of the Struma - a refugee ship that was torpedoed off the coast of Istanbul on February 24, 1942. The ship was carrying more than 750 Jewish refugees from Romania en route to Palestine. The book straddles two timelines - 2001 in Istanbul with flash backs to WW II times. A visiting professor from the U.S. travels to Istanbul University to spend a few days and is assigned a staff member - Maya Duran - to guide and assist him during his stay. But Max</span>
  <span id="freeText16699253787283365733" style="display:none">A lovely historical fiction based on the sinking of the Struma - a refugee ship that was torpedoed off the coast of Istanbul on February 24, 1942. The ship was carrying more than 750 Jewish refugees from Romania en route to Palestine. The book straddles two timelines - 2001 in Istanbul with flash backs to WW II times. A visiting professor from the U.S. travels to Istanbul University to spend a few days and is assigned a staff member - Maya Duran - to guide and assist him during his stay. But Maximilian Wagner is no ordinary professor - 59 years ago he lived in Istanbul…and 59 years ago is when he saw his wife, Nadia, for the last time. Over the course of a few days, Max’s story will unfold as Maya puts the pieces of the puzzle together - and relives for the reader the tragic story of Max and Nadia. So glad this book was translated into English - this is my second read by the author and I hope more of his books get translated soon. Another great read set in Turkey to add to my favorite reads list - highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16699253787283365733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3380861115" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3380861115" />
    <a title="Parsa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111732248-parsa"><img alt="Parsa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584895024p2/111732248.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3380861115?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Parsa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Parsa" href="/user/show/111732248-parsa">Parsa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3380861115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9212578762445178251">"<b>Serenade für Nadia</b>" is not so much a story as it is a <i>song</i>; a song of power and prejudice, of oppression and untold history. Livaneli does a fine job of retelling forgotten affairs and raveling the thin threads weaving human lives together through a series of emotional rollercoasters that gradually wear Maya, the protagonist <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[or is she? <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, down to the point where she forfeits the walls around her obscure world and sees her pre-established ethical cues as subject to c</span>
  <span id="freeText9212578762445178251" style="display:none">"<b>Serenade für Nadia</b>" is not so much a story as it is a <i>song</i>; a song of power and prejudice, of oppression and untold history. Livaneli does a fine job of retelling forgotten affairs and raveling the thin threads weaving human lives together through a series of emotional rollercoasters that gradually wear Maya, the protagonist <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[or is she? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, down to the point where she forfeits the walls around her obscure world and sees her pre-established ethical cues as subject to criticism, wisely disguised in a playful fling between progressive ideologies and unhinged anarchism set in modern-day Turkey, which, if nothing, is noticeably courageous of Livaneli. Maya entertains what she herself calls a <i>pseudo-philosophical</i> state of existential contemplation, narrated in a well-balanced fashion: slightly blunt so as not to exhaust the average reader, but also piercing enough to make one put down the book and simply <i>think</i>, from time to time.<br /><br />The emotional turmoil and the unceasing blows of grief and misery is told through the stories of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[three women from three different timelines all somehow adding a portion of their experiences to their young prodigy, Maya, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> which unfolds the horrific tales that have been unnaturally forgotten despite happening in the recent past.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["Hayatı zaten o küçük Karadeniz kıyısında bitmişdi; şimdi gecikmiş olan töreni yapılacaktı." <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />These blows hit hard. You <b>will</b> cry reading this. Trust me.<br /><br />Simply put, have <s>a few</s> lots of tissue packs around while reading and be ready for a decent philosophical and historical journey with a juicy texture rich in detail (which would most likely not be appealing to all tastes) peculiar to Livaneli, from Maya's everyday life routine to the story behind a random painting in the English embassy, and the ideology behind the government's infrastructural design.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9212578762445178251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781635420166" href="/book/show/52256788-serenade-for-nadia">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3224651681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer737143910879495478">Serenade For Nadia by Turkish writer Zulfu Livaneli, translated by Brendan Freely, is an historical fiction novel based on real life events between Turkey and Germany during World War II. <br/><br/>I am so grateful for this insightful, thoughtful, respectful novel that has the daunting task of retelling the 1942 tragedy of the Turkish ship Struma that was torpedoed by the Germans killing nearly 800 Jewish refugees on their way to Palestine.<br/><br/>The author opens in the year 2001 where we meet our narrator, Maya</span>
  <span id="freeText737143910879495478" style="display:none">Serenade For Nadia by Turkish writer Zulfu Livaneli, translated by Brendan Freely, is an historical fiction novel based on real life events between Turkey and Germany during World War II. <br /><br />I am so grateful for this insightful, thoughtful, respectful novel that has the daunting task of retelling the 1942 tragedy of the Turkish ship Struma that was torpedoed by the Germans killing nearly 800 Jewish refugees on their way to Palestine.<br /><br />The author opens in the year 2001 where we meet our narrator, Maya, who befriends a visiting professor who has come back to Turkey after decades of self imposed exile from the country that was the last home of his deceased wife. Though a curmudgeon old man, Maya not only comes to respect him but to understand his heartbreaking pain from a war that destroyed too many lives.<br /><br />Though this is a somber topic, and a moment in history I never heard of before reading this book, the author eloquently has us fall in love with a young couple in 1938 not aware of the pending tragedy in their future. There are times that the realism of this event makes the story feel more like a non fiction book. However, at times it is necessary to understand that this disaster was not an accident. That the horror was inflicted against human beings by human beings on purpose. <br /><br />One of the positive results of this book is that by creating characters that we care about the tragedy becomes more personal and more real. I also think having the current timeline in 2001 is a brilliant way of reminding us that there is still too much hate in this world and this time over 3, 000 people lost their lives on 9/11.<br /><br />Despite the sadness this is a necessary story. We need history to be told so we learn and never let it happen again. Like Maya, we learn from the past to enjoy and be grateful for the life we are living thanks to those who have sacrificed so much for us to be here now.<br /><br />I received a free copy of this book for a fair and honest review. All opinions are my own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="737143910879495478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3078628733" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3078628733" />
    <a title="Betty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3541694-betty"><img alt="Betty" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3078628733?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Betty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Betty" href="/user/show/3541694-betty">Betty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/48928025-serenade-for-nadia">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3541694-betty?shelf=jewish">jewish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3078628733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15824555919496454754">This is a beautifully written, heartbreaking story based on the real-life sinking of the Struma – a ship that launched from Romania and carried nearly 800 Jewish refugees on their way to Palestine. In February 1942, the ship was torpedoed while off the coast of Istanbul after being turned away by Turkish authorities.<br/><br/>The book is written with two timelines- one in 2001 with Maya Duran who is an employee of Istanbul University and her assignment of looking after Maximilian Wagner, a German-born Har</span>
  <span id="freeText15824555919496454754" style="display:none">This is a beautifully written, heartbreaking story based on the real-life sinking of the Struma – a ship that launched from Romania and carried nearly 800 Jewish refugees on their way to Palestine. In February 1942, the ship was torpedoed while off the coast of Istanbul after being turned away by Turkish authorities.<br /><br />The book is written with two timelines- one in 2001 with Maya Duran who is an employee of Istanbul University and her assignment of looking after Maximilian Wagner, a German-born Harvard professor. The other timeline is set during WWII and tells the love story of Max and Nadia, who were very much in love but were separated by the war. <br /><br />During her time with Max, Maya soon learns his true reason for returning to Istanbul after a 59-year absence. Slowly he reveals that he last saw his beloved wife Nadia 59 years ago there in Istanbul. Their love story is told with great passion but then veers into a horrific and heartrending conclusion. The past and the present collide leaving the reader emotionally drained. A true emotional rollercoaster.<br /><br />I must mention the brilliant translation done by Brendan Freely. He was able to maintain the magic of Livaneli’s writing throughout the story. The book also reveals some of the birthing pains of the Turkish nation itself, the atrocities committed against Armenians and Crimean Turks, the WWII politics between Turkey, Great Britain, and Russia. <br /><br />I enhanced my understanding of the historic event by watching the short documentary “The Search for the Struma” on YouTube.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15824555919496454754" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3395212780" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3395212780" />
    <a title="Doreen Fritz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1456404-doreen-fritz"><img alt="Doreen Fritz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275429997p2/1456404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3395212780?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Doreen Fritz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Doreen Fritz" href="/user/show/1456404-doreen-fritz">Doreen Fritz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781635420166" href="/book/show/52256788-serenade-for-nadia">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3395212780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16985053625065603900">Written by a noted Turkish author, this novel tells the story of two characters: an elderly German professor who returns to Turkey to say a last farewell to his long-dead wife who was killed during WWII, and the woman who is assigned to escort him around town during his visit to Istanbul. This woman, Maya, a divorced woman raising her teenage son, works for the University. She later writes about the professor and tells the story of both him and his wife. There are a lot of red-herring rambles th</span>
  <span id="freeText16985053625065603900" style="display:none">Written by a noted Turkish author, this novel tells the story of two characters: an elderly German professor who returns to Turkey to say a last farewell to his long-dead wife who was killed during WWII, and the woman who is assigned to escort him around town during his visit to Istanbul. This woman, Maya, a divorced woman raising her teenage son, works for the University. She later writes about the professor and tells the story of both him and his wife. There are a lot of red-herring rambles that are not really part of the story - is Professor Max a spy? Why are people following him? Why are people giving Maya sideways looks - do they believe the taxi driver and his stories about her carrying on an affair with this 87-year-old man? We also hear about Maya's grandmothers, and there is a lot written about Turkey's economy, history, racism, genocides, and current political scene. Sometimes it's hard for the author to stay focused on what is really the story. There are leaps in time, and no clear organization of his writing --- but all in all the storylines are interesting, and I do enjoy learning about other cultures. This was just so poorly constructed that I was distracted, and didn't enjoy it as much as I might have. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16985053625065603900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781635420166" href="/book/show/52256788-serenade-for-nadia">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6069769-rachel?shelf=jewishfiction2020">jewishfiction2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3231003107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer558742899288439130">Ever since my visit in 1995, I have been interested in Turkey and its Jewish community. So I was very excited to read this newly translated book by one of Turkey's bestselling authors. Livaneli's novel centers around Maya, a single mother who works for Istanbul University in 2001 and is assigned to host a visiting American professor, Max Wagner. During his visit, Maya learns about the many German (both Jewish and Nazi connected) academics who were recruited by the Turkish government to modernize</span>
  <span id="freeText558742899288439130" style="display:none">Ever since my visit in 1995, I have been interested in Turkey and its Jewish community. So I was very excited to read this newly translated book by one of Turkey's bestselling authors. Livaneli's novel centers around Maya, a single mother who works for Istanbul University in 2001 and is assigned to host a visiting American professor, Max Wagner. During his visit, Maya learns about the many German (both Jewish and Nazi connected) academics who were recruited by the Turkish government to modernize higher education as well as the Struma disaster which killed nearly 800 Jewish refugees trying to reach Palestine in 1942. She also learns about Max's wife Nadia. While the story was very interesting and I read the book quickly in 3 days, a few things bothered me. I'm not sure if it was the fault of the translator or because the author is a man, but I found his characterization of Maya very wooden and two-dimensional and her attitude towards her son, parenting, and motherhood not relatable or authentic. And I was totally shocked to read: "When does a girl stop growing up? . . . Life constantly changes her, and the principal agent of these changes is always a man." (p.385-386) I also felt like the author's research, while interesting and accessible, showed through too much. But, perhaps what bothered me most was that at several points in the story, Maya claims that she is Catholic, Muslim and Jewish. However, while we learn the tragic stories of her persecuted Armenian and Crimean grandparents, no one in her family was ever Jewish. She only feels Jewish after Max entrusted her with Nadia's story. I'm sorry, I don't buy it! And to me, this reeks of cultural appropriation. Would readers accept a character who claimed any other cultural/ethic/religious identity after simply learning a story about one individual? I doubt it. The story of the Struma needs to be told more but overall Serenade for Nadia was a disappointing read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="558742899288439130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3220184771" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3220184771" />
    <a title="Julie Failla Earhart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1277299-julie-failla-earhart"><img alt="Julie Failla Earhart" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3220184771?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie Failla Earhart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie Failla Earhart" href="/user/show/1277299-julie-failla-earhart">Julie Failla Earhart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781635420166" href="/book/show/52256788-serenade-for-nadia">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3220184771" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5813717857453934321">From one of Turkey’s bestselling authors, Zulfu Livaneli (don’t feel bad, I had never heard of him before either), comes a novel of an extraordinary love story mingled with a forgotten real-life tragedy intermingled with a spy-like thriller that is hard to put down. It’s a story-within a story-within a story that is virtually seamless for the reader. If you enjoyed the complexity of Margaret Atwood’s “The Blind Assassin,” I think you will geek-out with this novel.<br/><br/>Story One takes place on a plane</span>
  <span id="freeText5813717857453934321" style="display:none">From one of Turkey’s bestselling authors, Zulfu Livaneli (don’t feel bad, I had never heard of him before either), comes a novel of an extraordinary love story mingled with a forgotten real-life tragedy intermingled with a spy-like thriller that is hard to put down. It’s a story-within a story-within a story that is virtually seamless for the reader. If you enjoyed the complexity of Margaret Atwood’s “The Blind Assassin,” I think you will geek-out with this novel.<br /><br />Story One takes place on a plane in 2001. (Nothing to do with 9/11.) Maya Duran is headed from Istanbul to Boston to visit a professor that she in charge of escorting when he came to Istanbul University. While her plane-mates are sleeping, Maya wants to get the story she just lived down in writing. This part is not long and is interspersed through Story Two.<br /><br />Story Two finds Maya, a single mom who has a demanding job at Istanbul University with a teenage sone who spends more tiem on his computer that he does anything else. Maya has been selected to shepherd Professor Maximilan Wagner, now an elderly “German-born Harvard professor” who has come to lecture at Istanbul University. He brought with him one a bag and a violin.<br /><br />It has been fifty-nine years since Maximilan has been to Istanbul, not since the death of his wife in 1942, aboard the “Struma,” a shocking tragedy that “led to the death of nearly 800 refugees fleeing the Holocaust” for Palenstine. Max has one other reason for making the trip from Boston…he wants to play once more at the place he last saw his wife. However, when a white Renault begins to shadow them, Maya becomes nervous and starts to research Maximilan. She enlists the aid of her son, whose computer skills are invaluable. The scene of Maximilan playing one last time for his Nadia is nothing short of heartbreaking, so have tissues at hand. <br /><br />Story Three is Maximilian and Nadia’s story. I could feel the love they had for each other wrapping around my heart.<br /><br />Livaneli has created a story, or I should say stories, that will live within me for many days to come. “Serenade for Nadia” receives 5 out of 5 stars in Julie’s world. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5813717857453934321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sydnye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sydnye" href="/user/show/593798-sydnye">Sydnye</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3378470738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6683634985924101654">3.75. I received this book from Shelf Galley, gallery live of the week. While the history of the Struma and its occupants during WWII were fascinating history, the current day story of Maya and her involvement with an elderly Harvard professor did not ring as true. The author’s portrayal of her personality and as a mother did not work for me to view her as the heroine. While Livaneli tried to make us sympathetic to her political views, he failed to convince me that after just a few days Maya was</span>
  <span id="freeText6683634985924101654" style="display:none">3.75. I received this book from Shelf Galley, gallery live of the week. While the history of the Struma and its occupants during WWII were fascinating history, the current day story of Maya and her involvement with an elderly Harvard professor did not ring as true. The author’s portrayal of her personality and as a mother did not work for me to view her as the heroine. While Livaneli tried to make us sympathetic to her political views, he failed to convince me that after just a few days Maya was taking more risks for a stranger than were prudent at the expense of her safety and her son’s well being. Her flight notes at the end of each chapter made the reading disjointed. If I were only looking for an historical fiction novel, I would have rated it higher. The relationships did not work as well for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6683634985924101654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3376052931" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3376052931" />
    <a title="Josie Krieger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/88142282-josie-krieger"><img alt="Josie Krieger" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3376052931?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josie Krieger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josie Krieger" href="/user/show/88142282-josie-krieger">Josie Krieger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/48928025-serenade-for-nadia">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3376052931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11069263417070238240">I have never written a review for a book, but I felt compelled to do so because of my overall frustration with this piece. For such a historic injustice, I am disappointed in its retelling by Livaneli. I dare say I felt the character of Maya was quite shallow and I found it apparent that the story—revolving around the lives of multiple women—was written by a man. I saw other comments mention the sexism but my jaw dropped multiple times when I read certain lines. For example: "Life constantly cha</span>
  <span id="freeText11069263417070238240" style="display:none">I have never written a review for a book, but I felt compelled to do so because of my overall frustration with this piece. For such a historic injustice, I am disappointed in its retelling by Livaneli. I dare say I felt the character of Maya was quite shallow and I found it apparent that the story—revolving around the lives of multiple women—was written by a man. I saw other comments mention the sexism but my jaw dropped multiple times when I read certain lines. For example: "Life constantly changers her, and the principal agent of these changes is always a man" (pg. 385-386). In the middle of a story where a woman is uncovering the truth about her own family's secrets, systemic injustices, and inner conflict, the point to mention is that the biggest changes in her life has been... men??!? <br /><br />I would argue gives the men in her life far more credit than they deserve.<br /><br />Similarly, the fact that Maya's greatest conflict in the piece was a (SPOILER ALERT) sex scandal is beyond angering. Yes, the unequal focus on the sex lives of women in media is a real thing but, in a book about the Struma disaster and a woman uncovering her family's secret heritage... it's out of place and sexist. Women struggle with more than our sexual reputation. <br /><br />I give it two stars because the historical aspect of the book is fascinating and not often told, but overall I would not recommend reading this.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11069263417070238240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3245197163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6193247618586827200">I was glued to this book and felt tears at the end. Once again I learned about a whole new aspect of the scope of WWII Nazi Germany’s infiltration throughout the world. I had no idea that from 1939-1941, famous Jewish scientists fled from Nazi invaders to Turkey! Turkey had declared themselves neutral, however they were torn and coerced by both Nazi Germany and allied forces to side with them. Many scientists fled and were employed by the University of Istanbul. <br/>Maximilian Wagner, a famous scien</span>
  <span id="freeText6193247618586827200" style="display:none">I was glued to this book and felt tears at the end. Once again I learned about a whole new aspect of the scope of WWII Nazi Germany’s infiltration throughout the world. I had no idea that from 1939-1941, famous Jewish scientists fled from Nazi invaders to Turkey! Turkey had declared themselves neutral, however they were torn and coerced by both Nazi Germany and allied forces to side with them. Many scientists fled and were employed by the University of Istanbul. <br />Maximilian Wagner, a famous scientist, was not Jewish but his sweet wife Nadia was. He left first for Turkey and she was to follow but got picked up and taken to Dachau. Max was able, with his connections and liaison Priest in Istanbul, to have Nadia freed. He gets her a ticket on a so called luxury liner to come to Turkey. The ship’s name Struma.<br /><br />Book begins in 2001 with Maya writing about the visit of Max to Istanbul. (Max, now a Harvard professor, returning to Istanbul to deliver a speech at the University. His guide and University assigned coordinator is Maya).<br /><br />I cannot reveal more. Let me say that book moves back and forth from 2001 to 1939 era to Max’s return visit earlier in 2001. It transitions smoothly, offers much history of Turkey and Romania, as well as WWII horrors such as the ship Struma. It is based on factual history of events.<br /><br />This novel is well written and I highly recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6193247618586827200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer6396358751311288789">I read this in conjunction with Midnight at the Pera Palace, which made it even more interesting. Maya is Turkish and leads a pretty simple life. She is asked to escort a visiting professor from Harvard when he visits her Turkish University. This becomes a mysterious situation as he used to teach at that University and has come back to re-visit his memories of his life in Turkey. Along with some pieces of history that sometimes verge on "who cares" to the reader, the descriptions of Istanbul fro</span>
  <span id="freeText6396358751311288789" style="display:none">I read this in conjunction with Midnight at the Pera Palace, which made it even more interesting. Maya is Turkish and leads a pretty simple life. She is asked to escort a visiting professor from Harvard when he visits her Turkish University. This becomes a mysterious situation as he used to teach at that University and has come back to re-visit his memories of his life in Turkey. Along with some pieces of history that sometimes verge on "who cares" to the reader, the descriptions of Istanbul from the 30s to the present is quite interesting. We are pulled along with the mystery, which grows as the novel moves on.<br /><br />Mostly the translation works, but occasionally I felt a bit lost. The story is something not known by most people, regarding Jewish professors who were allowed to leave Nazi Germany to teach in Turkey. Sometimes sinister, sometimes lovely, I liked the book as a whole.</span>

Being aware and appreciating that Zulfu Livaneli, as an intellectual and well respected writer, scholar and artist, deliberately used an overly simplified narration, cliche opinions, not so good expressions and descriptions to reflect that the protagonist is NOT a writer (as she states in the last pages as well), I still can’t say that I enjoyed the literary aspect of the</span>
  <span id="freeText15119217266312933576" style="display:none">I enjoyed the book very much and learned/recalled many historic events, characters in addition to some traditional anecdotes. Being aware and appreciating that Zulfu Livaneli, as an intellectual and well respected writer, scholar and artist, deliberately used an overly simplified narration, cliche opinions, not so good expressions and descriptions to reflect that the protagonist is NOT a writer (as she states in the last pages as well), I still can’t say that I enjoyed the literary aspect of the book. Content 4.5 stars, writing 2 stars. Good book and should be easy to translate to other languages. I hope it will be and reach to as many people as possible.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4105695-meag-mckeron?shelf=wwii">wwii</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4105695-meag-mckeron?shelf=translation">translation</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3374059545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12029513849777379253">Overall a really beautiful, heartbreaking work. The writing was a bit clunky for my taste, but as the story moved a long I realized that’s the whole point - Maya is writing furiously, without edits or rethinking what she’s writing. She’s writing from the heart, and it’s interesting to watch her transform from a somewhat hard and self-absorbed lady into a compassionate woman willing to accept her own faults and help others. The history of Turkey during WWII was also interesting to read, as I knew</span>
  <span id="freeText12029513849777379253" style="display:none">Overall a really beautiful, heartbreaking work. The writing was a bit clunky for my taste, but as the story moved a long I realized that’s the whole point - Maya is writing furiously, without edits or rethinking what she’s writing. She’s writing from the heart, and it’s interesting to watch her transform from a somewhat hard and self-absorbed lady into a compassionate woman willing to accept her own faults and help others. The history of Turkey during WWII was also interesting to read, as I knew very little about it’s stance in the war and the atrocities that occurred there.</span>

          </span>

Although, at first I had the impression that this was a mediocre novel, I was caught by emotion and surprise after reading 50 pages of it. I do not know how but this book turned into an extremely personal experience of mine. One that I would only share with my better half... kudos to Livaneli.</span>

      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TiRgxonc/ico+WGBfmxFqT6hDCt5RTovlODXEdTNjYHGHZXV4ChaRKYab41eWC5pfIn+7/KZzmlZe3lqozhOBg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SETDppxsd4KAjsem8Hqq2RxJ0H6oQysXUcuTCGOBJEnAfTa19ZjT4Q5tyarQTsEZXmEiuiOf31GcUD1zFHTnzg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/714267.O_Z_Livaneli">About O.Z. Livaneli</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/714267.O_Z_Livaneli"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1480686700p3/714267.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/714267.O_Z_Livaneli">O.Z. Livaneli
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,056
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15400331777741742163">O.Z. Livaneli (in Turkish <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17853832.Z_lf__Livaneli' title='Zülfü Livaneli' rel='nofollow noopener'>Zülfü Livaneli</a>) born in 1946, is a singer, a composer, a bestselling Turkish author and a poet who is considered one of the most significant and influential authors and intellectuals of his time. His books have won numerous literary awards, both in his home country and abroad.<br/><br/>Although his novels are viewed as highly literary, Livaneli is considered the best selling contem</span>
  <span id="freeText15400331777741742163" style="display:none">O.Z. Livaneli (in Turkish <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17853832.Z_lf__Livaneli" title="Zülfü Livaneli" rel="nofollow noopener">Zülfü Livaneli</a>) born in 1946, is a singer, a composer, a bestselling Turkish author and a poet who is considered one of the most significant and influential authors and intellectuals of his time. His books have won numerous literary awards, both in his home country and abroad.<br /><br />Although his novels are viewed as highly literary, Livaneli is considered the best selling contemporary author of Turkey today. The article <i>A Festival of Musical Contrasts</i>, which appeared in the International New York Times (9.7.2014) refers to Zuflu Livaneli as a composer.<br /><br />Livaneli is known for his novels that interweave diverse social and historical backgrounds, figures, and incidents, such as in ‘Bliss’ which won the Barnes &amp; Noble's ‘Discovery of Great New Writers Award’ in 2006, and in his critically acclaimed ‘Serenade for Nadia’, ‘Leyla's House’, and ‘My Brother's Story’, which were all translated into 37 languages and won numerous Turkish and International literary awards, and were highly praised by prominent literary critics around the world. His novels have been turned into theatrical movies, stage plays, and operas.<br /><br />Livaneli was imprisoned several times during the 1971 Turkish coup d'état because of his political views and had to leave Turkey in 1972 and went on exile. He lived in Stockholm, Paris, Athens, and New York where he met and collaborated with artists and intellectuals such as Elia Kazan, Arthur Miller, James Baldwin, and Peter Ustinov among others. Livaneli returned to Turkey in 1984.<br /><br />His works and cultural and political activities and contributions to world peace were recognized by UNESCO in 1995 when he was appointed Goodwill Ambassador to UNESCO -- a post he still holds today. He served a term in the Turkish Parliament as well as in the Council of Europe.<br /><br />Livaneli is as accomplished as a writer as he is as a poet and a songwriter, cultural and political activist. Although he first became known for his contemporary music, Livaneli turned his focus to writing, in the last decades, when he realized that literature was closer to his heart. His first collection of short stories, 'A Child in Purgatory', published in 1978 was turned into a movie by Swedish and German TV.He is also a prominent social-democrat politician and was a member of the Turkish parliament for one term. Livaneli's novels have been turned into theatrical movies, stage plays, and operas.<br /><br />Livaneli is known for his contemporary music, in much the same way as Bob Dylan and his contemporaries in the United States were in the 60's. His 1997 Ankara concert was attended by no less than 500 thousand people. His collaborations with Mikis Theodorakis of Greece have been noted as a gesture of bringing together the two countries. Livaneli has been a UNESCO Goodwill Ambassador since 1996.<br /><br />Livaneli has composed some three hundred songs, a rhapsody recorded by London Symphony Orchestra–, and a ballet. His compositions have reached cult status nationwide and have been performed by internationally renowned artists such as Joan Baez, Maria Farantouri, María del Mar Bonet, Udo Lindenberg, Haris Alexiou, Jocelyn B. Smith, and Kate Westbrook. He has also written five plays and thirty film soundtracks. Among these soundtracks are the soundtrack for "Yol" (The Path), directed by Yilmaz Güney and winner of the Golden Palm in Cannes Film Festival, "The Herd", directed by Yılmaz Güney and Zeki Ökten, and "Shirin's Wedding" by German director Helma Sanders-Brahms. His recordings have been published in the USA, Sweden, Germany, Holland and France, and he has given dozens of concerts throughout the world. He has produced albums and performed with Mikis Theodorakis and Maria Farantouri, and he has also collaborated with Manos Hatzidakis, Giora Feidman, Inti-Illimani and Ángel Parra. In 2010, he sang 'Mothers of The Disappeared' with Bono at U2's concert in Istanbul, Turkey, which was U2's first-ever concert in Istanbul. Liv</span>
  <a data-text-id="15400331777741742163" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
